            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The emerging electrochem. energy storage systems beyond Li-ion batteries, including Na/K/Mg/Ca/Zn/Al-ion batteries, attract extensive interest as the development of Li-ion batteries is seriously hindered by the scarce Li resources.  During the past years, large amts. of studies have focused on the study of various electrode materials toward emerging metal-ion batteries to realize high energy d., high power d., and a long cycle life.  In particular, V-based nanomaterials have received great attention.  V-based compds. have a big family with different structures, chem. compns., and electrochem. properties, which provide huge possibilities for the development of emerging electrochem. energy storage.  In this review, a comprehensive overview of the recent progresses of promising V-based nanomaterials for emerging metal-ion batteries is presented.  The V-based materials are classified into four groups: V oxides, vanadates, V phosphates, and O-free V-based compds.  The structures, electrochem. properties, and modification strategies are discussed.  The structure-performance relations and charge storage mechanisms are focused on.  Finally, the perspectives about future directions of V-based nanomaterials for emerging energy storage devices are proposed.  This review will provide comprehensive knowledge of V-based nanomaterials and shed light on their potential applications in emerging energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqTA_FmH74ksbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liw9qDvuzID1w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXmt1SqtQ%253D%253D&amp;md5=02ae2332840446c0a2e6dbdbfb2021cd</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1021/nl500915b"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Niu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Meng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mai, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">VO<sub>2</sub> Nanowires Assembled into Hollow Microspheres for High-Rate and Long-Life Lithium Batteries</span>. <i>Nano Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>14</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2873</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2878</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">VO2 Nanowires Assembled into Hollow Microspheres for High-Rate and Long-Life Lithium Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Niu, Chaojiang; Meng, Jiashen; Han, Chunhua; Zhao, Kangning; Yan, Mengyu; Mai, Liqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2873-2878</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Development of 3-dimensional nanostructures with high surface area and excellent structural stability is an important approach for realizing high-rate and long-life battery electrodes.  Here, the authors report VO2 hollow microspheres showing empty spherical core with radially protruding nanowires, synthesized through a facile and controllable ion-modulating approach.  By controlling the self-assembly of neg. charged C12H25SO4- spherical micelles and pos. charged VO2+ ions, 6-armed microspindles and random nanowires are also prepd.  Compared with them, VO2 hollow microspheres show better electrochem. performance.  At high c.d. of 2 A/g, VO2 hollow microspheres exhibit 3 times higher capacity than that of random nanowires, and 80% of the original capacity is retained after 1000 cycles.  The superior performance of VO2 hollow microspheres is because they exhibit high surface area about twice higher than that of random nanowires and also provide an efficient self-expansion and self-shrinkage buffering during lithiation/delithiation, which effectively inhibits the self-aggregation of nanowires.  This research indicates that VO2 hollow microspheres have great potential for high-rate and long-life Li batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqq0KAZ6rbRvrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liw9qDvuzID1w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXmtlSnsrg%253D&amp;md5=42b19b7343425adc3ef9ac45ac83c56d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1039/C8TA11419F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ye, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mei, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, R.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A 3D Flower-Like VO<sub>2</sub>/MXene Hybrid Architecture with Superior Anode Performance for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A 3D flower-like VO2/MXene hybrid architecture with superior anode performance for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Feng; Jiang, Ying; Ye, Zhengqing; Huang, Yongxin; Wang, Ziheng; Li, Shuaijie; Mei, Yang; Xie, Man; Li, Li; Chen, Renjie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">VO2 is considered to be a promising sodium ion storage material owing to its high specific capacity.  However, the cycling stability and rate performance obtained from this material are still unsatisfactory, as a result of inferior electronic cond. and significant vol. expansion during the charge/discharge process.  Herein, we report a VO2/MXene hybrid having a three-dimensional (3D) flower-like architecture, synthesized via a facile hydrothermal method.  Based on the synergistic effect of the VO2 and MXene, this material exhibits superior sodium storage behavior.  When used as an anode in sodium ion batteries, the as-prepd. VO2/MXene demonstrates a high reversible capacity of 280.9 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 0.1 A g-1, exceptional cycling life (141% capacity retention over 200 cycles at 0.1 A g-1) and good rate capacity (206 mA h g-1 at 1.6 A g-1).  This VO2/MXene hybrid therefore shows promise as an anode material for use in sodium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGobkOJvzCBQarVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liw9qDvuzID1w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXisF2ht73O&amp;md5=9db23e96de8bb1c0c8e345c48f563900</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201803594"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rozier, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Alshareef, H.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors study Na/Li-ion diffusion and electrochem. performance of NaVO3 (NVO) as anode material in Na/Li-ion batteries with the specific capacity of ≈350 mAhg-1 at the c.d. 11 mAg-1 after 300 cycles for Li-ion battery.  Remarkably, the capacity retains ≥200 mAhg-1 even after 400 cycles at 44 mAg-1 with Coulombic efficiency and amp;gt;99%.  The deduced diffusion coeff. from galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique (GITT), electrochem. impedance spectroscopy (EIS) and cyclic voltammetry (CV) measurements for NVO as anode in Li-ion battery is at 10-10-10-12 cm2s-1.  In case of Na-ion batteries, the NVO electrode exhibits initial capacity of 385 mAhg-1 at 7 mAg-1 current rate, but the capacity degrdn. is relatively faster in subsequent cycles.  The diffusion coeff. of NVO-Na cells similar to that of NVO-Li were found.  However, the authors' charge discharge measurements suggest that the overall performance of NVO anode is better in Li-ion battery than Na-ion.  Also, the authors use the d. functional theory to simulate the energetics of Na vacancy formation or addn. in the bulk of the NVO structure, which is 0.9-1.2 eV higher than that of the most stable (100) surface.  Thus, the Na ion incorporation at the surface of the electrode material is more facile compared to the bulk.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpLzpyZoBoQjrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljWH5jodT_sqQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Phosphorus-Functionalized Fe2VO4/Nitrogen-Doped Carbon Mesoporous Nanowires with Exceptional Lithium Storage Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tao, Yuanxue; Yang, Nan; Liang, Chennan; Huang, Dekang; Wang, Pei; Cao, Feifei; Luo, Yanzhu; Chen, Hao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ChemElectroChem</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The binary transition metal oxides have attracted great attention because of their considerable energy and power densities.  However, they suffer from low reaction kinetics and large vol. change, limiting their practical energy applications.  The construction of a mesoporous structure with a large surface area, the development of a carbon matrix, as well as heteroatom doping can effectively overcome the above challenges.  Herein, the synthesis of phosphorous-contg. Fe2VO4/nitrogen-doped carbon mesoporous nanowires (P-Fe2VO4/NCMNWs) is reported.  In this unique structure, the at.-level P-doping could increase the cond. of Fe2VO4 by reducing its band gap, which is confirmed by DFT calcns.  Furthermore, the phosphorus can covalently "bridge" the carbon layer and Fe2VO4 through P-C and Fe-O-P bondings.  As a result, this anode material exhibits a high capacity (1002 mA h g-1 at 0.5 A g-1 after 250 cycles), excellent rate performance (448 mA h g-1 at 10 A g-1), and prominent long-term cycling stability (533 mA h g-1 at 5 A g-1 after 500 cycles, 364 mA h g-1 at 10 A g-1 after 1000 cycles).  All of these attractive features make the P-Fe2VO4/NCMNWs a promising electrode material for high-performance lithium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo5BtJv1ze-3rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljWH5jodT_sqQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXlslGksr8%253D&amp;md5=0653771b80a602ca69f97738f8227945</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1007/s11581-019-03308-7"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Microwave Hydrothermal Synthesis of SbVO<sub>4</sub> Nanospheres as Anode Materials for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Ionics</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>26</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1267</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1273</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sb-based compds. are regarded as promising anode materials for sodium ion batteries (SIBs).                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Thermodynamic analysis and kinetic optimization of high-energy batteries based on multi-electron reactions</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Yong-Xin; Wu, Feng; Chen, Ren-Jie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">National Science Review</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Oxford University Press</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Multi-electron reaction can be regarded as an effective way of building high-energy systems (&gt;500 W h kg-1).  However, some confusions hinder the development of multi-electron mechanisms, such as clear concept, complex reaction, material design and electrolyte optimization and full-cell fabrication.  Therefore, this review discusses the basic theories and application bottlenecks of multi-electron mechanisms from the view of thermodn. and dynamic principles.  In future, high-energy batteries, metal anodes and multi-electron cathodes are promising electrode materials with high theor. capacity and high output voltage.  While the primary issue for the multi-electron transfer process is sluggish kinetics, which may be caused by multiple ionic migration, large ionic radius, high reaction energy barrier, low electron cond., poor structural stability, etc., it is urgent that feasible and versatile modification methods are summarized and new inspiration proposed in order to break through kinetic constraints.                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemical reaction of lithium with nanosized vanadium antimonate</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Morales, Julian; Sanchez, Luis; Martin, Francisco; Berry, Frank</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Solid State Chemistry</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nanoparticle VSbO4 was prepd. by mech. milling of Sb2O3 and V2O5 - it was characterized by XRD, TEM, Mossbauer spectroscopy and XPS.  Its reactivity towards Li was examd. by testing Li/VSbO4 cells under galvanostatic and potentiostatic regimes.  The amt. of Li inserted is consistent with a 2-step process involving the reactions (a) VSbO4+8Li → Sb+V+4Li2O and (b) Sb+3Li → Li3Sb, the former being virtually irreversible and the latter reversible as suggested by the shape of the anodic and cathodic curves.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The different Li/Na ion storage mechanisms of nano Sb2O3 anchored on graphene</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Hai; Qian, Kun; Qin, Xianying; Liu, Dongqing; Shi, Ruiying; Ran, Aihua; Han, Cuiping; He, Yan-Bing; Kang, Feiyu; Li, Baohua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">385</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The antimony oxide/reduced graphene oxide (Sb2O3/rGO) nanocomposites are used as anode of Li-ion and Na-ion batteries (LIBs and NIBs).  However, it is unclear about Li-ion and Na-ion storage mechanism in Sb2O3/rGO nanocomposites.  Herein, the conversion-alloying mechanisms of Sb2O3/rGO anodes for Na-ion and Li-ion storage are comparatively studied with a combined in-situ XRD and quasi in-situ XPS method.  The distinct behaviors are monitored during (de)lithiation and (de)sodiation with respect to crystal structure and chem. compn. evolution.  It is evidenced that the Na-ion can be easily transported to the inner part of the Sb2O3, where the Li-ion almost cannot reach, leading to a fully transformation during sodiation.  In addn., the conversion reaction product of amorphous Na2O display their better chem. stability than amorphous Li2O during electrochem. cycles, which contribute to a stable and long cycling life of NIBs.  This work gain insight into the high-capacity anodes with conversation-alloying mechanism for NIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqYH6L4bixii7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhJbyWeafE3hQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXltVKkurY%253D&amp;md5=2801580dae4365a2e10c3bdd3b4bb313</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1039/C9TA07508A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ouyang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Phosphorus and Carbon Composite Containing Nanocrystalline Sb as a Stable and High-Capacity Anode for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A phosphorus and carbon composite containing nanocrystalline Sb as a stable and high-capacity anode for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Miao; Ouyang, Liuzhang; Zhu, Min; Fang, Fang; Liu, Jiangwen; Liu, Zongwen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">443-452</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries are a potential alternative to lithium ion batteries due to the low cost and natural abundance of sodium.  In this study, the synthesis is demonstrated of a ternary Sb/P-C composite by using facile discharge plasma-assisted milling (P-milling) to combine Sb and high theor. specific capacity red phosphorus (RP).  The high hardness Sb particles facilitated the refinement of the P particles and exfoliated expanded graphite during the P-milling process, while the rapid heating by plasma promoted the refinement of Sb and P particles.  Ultimately, the cryst. Sb nanograins were well-dispersed in the amorphous P and C matrix, and the P and C components were connected by the P-C bonds.  This unique structure ensures a strong electrode structural integrity and ultra-fast electron transport during cycling.  As a result, the Sb/P-C composite delivered a high av. initial coulombic efficiency of 73.5%, and a reversible capacity of 596 mA h g-1 after 300 cycles at 1.0 A g-1, a very impressive performance among the reported P-based materials.  The present approach provides a new strategy for the prepn. of anode materials of high capacity and long cycle life for sodium-ion batteries and other energy storage systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrmDND1n2Yqi7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhJbyWeafE3hQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Curbing polysulfide shuttling by synergistic engineering layer composed of supported Sn4P3 nanodots electrocatalyst in lithium-sulfur batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ye, Zhengqing; Jiang, Ying; Feng, Tao; Wang, Ziheng; Li, Li; Wu, Feng; Chen, Renjie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">70</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">104532</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The shuttle effect in lithium-sulfur (Li-S) batteries mainly originates from the diffusion of sol. polysulfides (LiPSs) and their depressed redox kinetics.  Herein, we report a synergistic engineering layer composed of acorn shell porous carbon/Sn4P3 nanodots electrocatalyst (AS PC-Sn4P3).  The synergistic engineering layer can not only serve as a conductive interface but also provide a dual-adsorption barrier to retain active material and inhibit the LiPSs migrating.  More importantly, electrocatalytic Sn4P3 nanodots supported on acorn shell porous carbon (AS PC) within synergistic engineering layer effectively promote lithium ion diffusion, LiPSs conversion, Li2S2/Li2S deposition, and accelerate the electrochem. redox reaction and therefore curb the sol. LiPSs shutting behavior.  As a result, enhanced Li-S battery performance is achieved with synergistic engineering layer, e.g., excellent cycling stability over 900 cycles at 1.0C with a low capacity decay of 0.046% per cycle, a good rate performance, and a high areal capacity of 8.7 mAh cm-2 under lean electrolyte conditions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqNzMLE1rhpJLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhJbyWeafE3hQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Novel Polygonal Vanadium Oxide Nanoscrolls as Stable Cathode for Lithium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wei, Qiulong; Tan, Shuangshuang; Liu, Xiaoyi; Yan, Mengyu; Wang, Fengchao; Li, Qidong; An, Qinyou; Sun, Ruimin; Zhao, Kangning; Wu, Hengan; Mai, Liqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Scroll-shape structures with adjustable space provide interlayer sliding to accommodate the vol. changes, which are promising candidates for increasing the stability of lithium batteries (LBs).  In this work, for the first time, novel vanadium oxide polygonal nanoscrolls (PNSs) are synthesized in soln. through self-rolling, Ostwald ripening, and scroll-by-scroll processes.  The PNSs are of various shapes (including triangle, quadrangle, pentagon, and so forth) and spiral-wrapped multiwall.  When evaluated as cathode for LB, the vanadium oxide PNSs cathode exhibits largely enhanced cycling stability (capacity retention of 91.7% after 150 cycles at 0.1 A g-1 in 2.0-4.0 V) compared with those of nonscrolled nanobelts (40.0%) and nanowires (35.8%).  Even at 1.0 A g-1, the PNSs cathode delivers high-rate long-life performance with capacity retention of 80.6% after 500 cycles.  The unique polygonal nanoscroll structure is favorable for improving the cyclability and rate capability in energy storage applications as demonstrated here, and it will be interesting and has great potential for other related applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoHBf1-KOs2v7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg-HZIKJ1A7yA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXkvF2gtLw%253D&amp;md5=578f334b33817f48ddacd94e431842f0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1039/C7DT03188B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">SbVO<sub>4</sub> Nanoparticles Synthesized via Three Facile One-Pot Methods: Controllable Morphologies and Superhydrophobic Coatings</span>. <i>Dalton Trans.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>46</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">12988</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">12995</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Inert colloidal SbVO4 with special morphologies is promising for practical superhydrophobic coatings.  However, its conventional synthesis suffers from harsh prepn. conditions, limiting the material applications.  Herein, by using K6V10O28·9H2O as a novel vanadium source, SbVO4 nanoparticles were prepd. through three different facile methods: hydrothermal method, reflux method and ultrasonic method.  The pH values of the reaction environment were tuned as the only variable to shape the final products.  Colloidal morphologies can be engineered to microflakes, or amalgamations of nanoparticles.  Drop-casting glasses with the as-synthesized samples will lead to surface superhydrophobicity under basic, neutral, and acidic conditions.  Static contact angle of as-coated film can reach above 160° and be durable even under salt soln. of different pH values.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Biomimetic Sn4P3 Anchored on Carbon Nanotubes as an Anode for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ran, Lingbing; Luo, Bin; Gentle, Ian R.; Lin, Tongen; Sun, Qiang; Li, Ming; Rana, Md Masud; Wang, Lianzhou; Knibbe, Ruth</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Recently, Sn4P3 has emerged as a promising anode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to the high specific capacity.  However, the use of Sn4P3 has been impeded by capacity fade and an inferior rate performance.  Herein, a biomimetic heterostructure is reported by using a simple hydrothermal reaction followed by thermal treatment.  This bottlebrush-like structure consists of a stem-like carbon nanotube (CNT) as the electron expressway and mech. support; fructus-like Sn4P3 nanoparticles as the active material; and the permeable stoma-like thin carbon coating as the buffer layer.  Having benefited from the biomimetic structure, a superior electrochem. performance is obtained in the SIBs.  It exhibits a high capacity of 742 mA h g-1 after 150 cycles at 0.2C, and superior rate performance with 449 mA h g-1 at 2C after 500 cycles.  Moreover, the sodium storage mechanism is confirmed by cyclic voltammetry and ex situ X-ray diffraction and transmission electron microscopy.  In situ electrochem. impedance spectroscopy was adopted to analyze the reaction dynamics.  This research represents a further step toward figuring out the inferior electrochem. performance of other metal phosphide materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqi0vlL0Pw9D7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg-HZIKJ1A7yA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhsVSiu7bP&amp;md5=521acacd64cd8786ae3120281a0139d9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.7b10107"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lv, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lei, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sb<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> Nanoparticles Anchored on Graphene Sheets via Alcohol Dissolution-Reprecipitation Method for Excellent Lithium-Storage Properties</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen and oxygen-codoped carbon nanospheres for excellent specific capacitance and cyclic stability supercapacitor electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ye, Zhengqing; Wang, Feijun; Jia, Chao; Mu, Keguang; Yu, Miao; Lv, Yanyan; Shao, Ziqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

All the O, N-codoped activated carbon aerogels exhibit 3D interconnected hierarchical porous network structures with high sp. surface areas (1337-1695 m2 g-1), ultramicropores (0.52-0.54 nm), and rich O (12.68-18.48%) and N (1.18-3.59%) doping.  A typical 3D O, N-codoped activated carbon aerogel (ACA700) obtained at the activation of 700 °C exhibits excellent electrochem. performance.  When ACA700 is utilized as electrode materials for supercapacitor, the highest specific capacitance of 342 F g-1 at a c.d. of 2 A g-1 in 3 M H2SO4 electrolyte is achieved.  Furthermore, ACA700//ACA700 all-solid-state supercapacitor device displays acceptable energy d. (3.8 Wh kg-1) at a power d. of 246.0 W kg-1, extraordinary coulombic efficiency (95.8%), and good rate capability.  Therefore, the sustainable 3D O, N-codoped activated carbon aerogels with ultramicropores demonstrate tremendous potential for energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqBodfXX4kDYLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhbVj4ndoUuVg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtVCnt7bI&amp;md5=1844ba37daebf7bd9fe83defa62d27ad</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA02689G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Choi, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sb<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/MXene(Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>Tx) Hybrid Anode Materials with Enhanced Performance for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sb2O3/MXene(Ti3C2Tx) hybrid anode materials with enhanced performance for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Guo, Xin; Xie, Xiuqiang; Choi, Sinho; Zhao, Yufei; Liu, Hao; Wang, Chengyin; Chang, Song; Wang, Guoxiu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">24</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">12445-12452</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">MXenes, a novel family of two dimensional (2D) materials with excellent electronic cond. and hydrophilicity, have emerged as a promising material for energy storage.  Based on the intercalation mechanism, MXenes have demonstrated an excellent performance for supercapacitors but low capacities for sodium-ion batteries.  Herein, we developed a facile soln.-phase method to fabricate the Sb2O3/MXene(Ti3C2Tx) hybrid materials for sodium storage with enhanced electrochem. performances.  The as-prepd. Sb2O3/Ti3C2Tx composite has a hierarchical structure with Sb2O3 nanoparticles (sub-50 nm) uniformly incorporated in the MXene Ti3C2Tx 3D networks.  The Sb2O3 nanoparticles serve as a sufficient sodium ion reservoir; meanwhile, the MXene Ti3C2Tx network provides highly efficient pathways for transport of electrons and Na-ions.  The vol. expansion of Sb2O3 during sodiation/desodiation can be buffered and confined between the 2D Ti3C2Tx sheets.  As a result, the Sb2O3/Ti3C2Tx hybrid anodes present good structural stability and superior electrochem. performance in Na-ion batteries, including an excellent rate performance with a capacity of 295 mA h g-1 at 2 A g-1, and an enhanced cycling performance with a capacity of 472 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles at 100 mA g-1.  This work is expected to inspire the development of MXene materials for high performance batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGooUt2Gvc4nKbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhbVj4ndoUuVg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXot1ejtb4%253D&amp;md5=79ba612eb8fed1557a31b5e925541349</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1002/celc.201800618"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sheng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Micro/Nanostructure-Dependent Electrochemical Performances of Sb<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> Micro-Bundles as Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ChemElectroChem</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2522</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2527</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Micro/Nanostructure-Dependent Electrochemical Performances of Sb2O3 Micro-Bundles as Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Leping; Huang, Yuli; Li, Xiaoyun; Sheng, Jian; Li, Feng; Xie, Zhaojun; Zhou, Zhen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ChemElectroChem</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries (SIBs) are regarded as promising next-generation energy storage devices due to their decent theor. energy d. and esp. low cost.  Here, micro/nanostructured Sb2O3 micro-bundles consisting of many abreast nanoribbons were prepd. via a simple hydrothermal route.  In this unique structure, both ends of Sb2O3 nanoribbons with the thickness of ∼50 nm scatter with each other and extend radially from the center point, which not only reserves more space between nanoribbons to accommodate vol. changes, but also provides plenty of open channels to facilitate the intimate contact of active species, conductive agents and electrolytes, thus efficiently shortening diffusion paths of Na+/e-.  Evaluated as anode materials for SIBs, Sb2O3 micro-bundles delivered outstanding electrochem. performance: high reversible capacity, superb rate capability, and stable cyclic ability.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhancing Sodium Ion Battery Performance by Strongly Binding Nanostructured Sb2S3 on Sulfur-Doped Graphene Sheets</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiong, Xunhui; Wang, Guanhua; Lin, Yuwei; Wang, Ying; Ou, Xing; Zheng, Fenghua; Yang, Chenghao; Wang, Jeng-Han; Liu, Meilin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na ion batteries (SIBs) have been considered a promising alternative to Li ion batteries for large-scale energy storage.  However, their inferior electrochem. performances, esp. cyclability, become the major challenge for further development of SIBs.  Large vol. change and sluggish diffusion kinetics are generally considered to be responsible for the fast capacity degrdn.  We report the strong chem. bonding of nanostructured Sb2S3 on S-doped graphene sheets (Sb2S3/SGS) that enables a stable capacity retention of 83% for 900 cycles with high capacities and excellent rate performances.  To the best of our knowledge, the cycling performance of the Sb2S3/SGS composite is superior to those reported for any other Sb-based materials for SIBs.  Computational calcns. demonstrate that S-doped graphene (SGS) has a stronger affinity for Sb2S3 and the discharge products than pure graphene, resulting in a robust composite architecture for outstanding cycling stability.  Our study shows a feasible and effective way to solve the long-term cycling stability issue for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqCGE30ZIPm4bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhbVj4ndoUuVg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Exceptional adsorption and catalysis effects of hollow polyhedra/carbon nanotube confined CoP nanoparticles superstructures for enhanced lithium-sulfur batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ye, Zhengqing; Jiang, Ying; Qian, Ji; Li, Wanlong; Feng, Tao; Li, Li; Wu, Feng; Chen, Renjie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">64</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Lithium-sulfur (Li-S) batteries with high theor. energy d. are promising next-generation green energy storage devices.  However, the severe shuttling and depressed conversion of lithium polysulfides in sulfur cathode are two pivotal factors that limit the practical application of Li-S batteries.  To solve these issues, rationally designed hollow polyhedra/carbon nanotube confined CoP nanoparticles superstructures (CoP@HPCN) for enhanced Li-S batteries are proposed here.  With the high porosity and cavity, and multidirectional channels, hollow polyhedra/carbon nanotube architecture can effectively accommodate vol. expansion and entrap sulfur species.  More importantly, the exptl. and theor. results indicate that the uniformly inserted polar CoP nanoparticles as electrocatalyst not only significantly anchor polysulfides, but also catalyze the transformation of lithium polysulfides.  Benefiting from these advantages, the CoP@HPCN based sulfur cathode can achieve good rate performance, impressive cycling stability, and ultralow self-discharge const. of 0.03% per day after resting for 60 days even at high sulfur loading of 3.7 mg cm-2.  This work synergistically combines desired design and electrocatalysis in sulfur electrode and sheds some light on the construction of advanced Li-S batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqlZ1vJ5Z-rp7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhbVj4ndoUuVg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhsFGjsLvO&amp;md5=366291ef2f391836252eba32fbedf795</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1038/35035045"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Poizot, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Laruelle, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Grugeon, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dupont, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tarascon, J.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nano-sized transition-metal oxides as negative-electrode materials for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Poizot P; Laruelle S; Grugeon S; Dupont L; Tarascon J M</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2000</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">407</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6803</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">496-9</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0028-0836</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable solid-state batteries have long been considered an attractive power source for a wide variety of applications, and in particular, lithium-ion batteries are emerging as the technology of choice for portable electronics.  One of the main challenges in the design of these batteries is to ensure that the electrodes maintain their integrity over many discharge-recharge cycles.  Although promising electrode systems have recently been proposed, their lifespans are limited by Li-alloying agglomeration or the growth of passivation layers, which prevent the fully reversible insertion of Li ions into the negative electrodes.  Here we report that electrodes made of nanoparticles of transition-metal oxides (MO, where M is Co, Ni, Cu or Fe) demonstrate electrochemical capacities of 700 mA h g(-1), with 100% capacity retention for up to 100 cycles and high recharging rates.  The mechanism of Li reactivity differs from the classical Li insertion/deinsertion or Li-alloying processes, and involves the formation and decomposition of Li2O, accompanying the reduction and oxidation of metal nanoparticles (in the range 1-5 nanometres) respectively.  We expect that the use of transition-metal nanoparticles to enhance surface electrochemical reactivity will lead to further improvements in the performance of lithium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcTITCWEoR0MQxfKb6ELK8t0fW6udTcc2eYX2xpo25riv7ntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BD3cvnslKhtQ%253D%253D&amp;md5=5a244324b84031fe58b67cdc4038c56c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201202623"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Reconstruction of Conformal Nanoscale MnO on Graphene as a High-Capacity and Long-Life Anode Material for Lithium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Reconstruction of Conformal Nanoscale MnO on Graphene as a High-Capacity and Long-Life Anode Material for Lithium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Yongming; Hu, Xianluo; Luo, Wei; Xia, Fangfang; Huang, Yunhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">23</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">19</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2436-2444</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">To tackle the issue of inferior cycle stability and rate capability for MnO anode materials in lithium ion batteries, a facile strategy is explored to prep. a hybrid material consisting of MnO nanocrystals grown on conductive graphene nanosheets.  The prepd. MnO/graphene hybrid anode exhibits a reversible capacity as high as 2014.1 mAh g-1 after 150 discharge/charge cycles at 200 mA g-1, excellent rate capability (625.8 mAh g-1 at 3000 mA g-1), and superior cyclability (843.3 mAh g-1 even after 400 discharge/charge cycles at 2000 mA g-1 with only 0.01% capacity loss per cycle).  The results suggest that the reconstruction of the MnO/graphene electrodes is intrinsic due to conversion reactions.  A long-term stable nanoarchitecture of graphene-supported ultrafine manganese oxide nanoparticles is formed upon cycling, which yields a long-life anode material for lithium ion batteries.  The lithiation and delithiation behavior suggests that the further oxidn. of Mn(II) to Mn(IV) and the interfacial lithium storage upon cycling contribute to the enhanced specific capacity.  The excellent rate capability benefits from the presence of conductive graphene and a short transportation length for both lithium ions and electrons.  Moreover, the as-formed hybrid nanostructure of MnO on graphene may help achieve faster kinetics of conversion reactions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqSjyTOe_ODXLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh6-2IPRR4aSw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhvVWnsL%252FE&amp;md5=993266e37afcdc7949e8735381125094</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.7b03321"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ge, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Miao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">ZnS-Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>@C Core-Double Shell Polyhedron Structure Derived from Metal-Organic Framework as Anodes for High Performance Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>11</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">6474</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">6482</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">ZnS-Sb2S3@C Core-Double Shell Polyhedron Structure Derived from Metal-Organic Framework as Anodes for High Performance Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dong, Shihua; Li, Caixia; Ge, Xiaoli; Li, Zhaoqiang; Miao, Xianguang; Yin, Longwei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6474-6482</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Taking advantage of zeolitic imidazolate framework (ZIF-8), ZnS-Sb2S3@C core-double shell polyhedron structure is synthesized through a sulfurization reaction between Zn2+ dissocd. from ZIF-8 and S2- from thioacetamide (TAA), and subsequently a metal cation exchange process between Zn2+ and Sb3+, in which carbon layer is introduced from polymeric resorcinol-formaldehyde to prevent the collapse of the polyhedron.  The polyhedron composite with a ZnS inner-core and Sb2S3/C double-shell as anode for sodium ion batteries (SIBs) shows us a significantly improved electrochem. performance with stable cycle stability, high Coulombic efficiency and specific capacity.  Peculiarly, introducing a carbon shell not only acts as an important protective layer to form a rigid construction and accommodate the vol. changes, but also improves the electronic cond. to optimize the stable cycle performance and the excellent rate property.  The architecture composed of ZnS inner core and a complex Sb2S3/C shell not only facilitates the facile electrolyte infiltration to reduce the Na-ion diffusion length to improve the electrochem. reaction kinetics, but also prevents the structure pulverization caused by Na-ion insertion/extn.  This approach to prep. metal sulfides based on MOFs can be further extended to design other nanostructured systems for high performance energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq4CDXhsDn8x7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh6-2IPRR4aSw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXpslCltrs%253D&amp;md5=4c74722fd5ce6e89694ff153fed88cee</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1021/ja310347x"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Darwiche, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Marino, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sougrati, M.                 10.1021/ja310347x</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D134%26publication_year%3D2012%26pages%3D20805-20811%26journal%3DJ.%2BAm.%2BChem.%2BSoc.%26author%3DA.%2BDarwiche%26author%3DC.%2BMarino%26author%3DM.%2BT.%2BSougrati%26author%3DB.%2BFraisse%26author%3DL.%2BStievano%26author%3DL.%2BMonconduit%26title%3DBetter%2BCycling%2BPerformances%2Bof%2BBulk%2BSb%2Bin%2BNa-Ion%2BBatteries%2BCompared%2Bto%2BLi-Ion%2BSystems%253A%2BAn%2BUnexpected%2BElectrochemical%2BMechanism%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fja310347x&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.0c21676&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fja310347x&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Better Cycling Performances of Bulk Sb in Na-Ion Batteries Compared to Li-Ion Systems: An Unexpected Electrochemical Mechanism</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Darwiche, Ali; Marino, Cyril; Sougrati, Moulay T.; Fraisse, Bernard; Stievano, Lorenzo; Monconduit, Laure</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">134</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">51</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">20805-20811</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pure micrometric antimony can be successfully used as neg. electrode material in Na-ion batteries, sustaining a capacity close to 600 mAh g-1 at a high rate with a Coulombic efficiency of 99 over 160 cycles, an extremely high capacity compared to any other compd. tested against both Li and Na.  The reaction mechanism with Na does not simply go through the alloying mechanism obsd. for Li where the intermediate species are those expected from the phase diagram.  In the case of Na, the intermediate phases are mostly amorphous and could not be precisely identified.  Surprisingly, it is evidenced that a competition takes place at the end of the discharge of the Sb/Na cell between the formation of the hexagonal and the cubic polymorphs of Na3Sb, the last being described in the literature as unstable at atm. pressure and only synthesized under high pressure (1-9 GPa).  In addn., fluoroethylene carbonate added to the electrolyte combined with an appropriate electrode formulation based on CM-cellulose, carbon black, and vapor ground carbon fibers seems to be determinant in the excellent performances of this material.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpfZ6rvnJyfxrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh6-2IPRR4aSw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhslCgsbnE&amp;md5=75362e7708fe6434655290ce0aa7cac0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2019.03.244"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sb<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub>/Co-Containing Carbon Polyhedra as Anode Material for High-Performance Lithium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem. Eng. J.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>370</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">800</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">809</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.cej.2019.03.244</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D370%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D800-809%26journal%3DChem.%2BEng.%2BJ.%26author%3DJ.%2BLi%26author%3DL.%2BHan%26author%3DX.%2BZhang%26author%3DG.%2BZhu%26author%3DT.%2BChen%26author%3DT.%2BLu%26author%3DL.%2BPan%26title%3DSb2O5%252FCo-Containing%2BCarbon%2BPolyhedra%2Bas%2BAnode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BHigh-Performance%2BLithium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.cej.2019.03.244&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.0c21676&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.cej.2019.03.244&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sb2O5/Co-containing carbon polyhedra as anode material for high-performance lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Junfeng; Han, Lu; Zhang, Xiaojie; Zhu, Guang; Chen, Taiqiang; Lu, Ting; Pan, Likun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">370</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">800-809</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMEJAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1385-8947</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony-based oxides (SbxOy) were considered as promising candidate anode materials for lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  However, the poor elec. cond. and huge vol. change of SbxOy during lithium insertion and extn. hinder its lithium-storage performance.  Sb2O5/Co-contg. carbon polyhedra (SCCP) were prepd. through a galvanic replacement reaction accompanied by oxidn. process.  Sb2O5 possesses high theor. capacity and carbon not only effectively improves the charge transport ability but also accommodates the vol. change of Sb2O5 during charge/discharge process.  Besides, the inner metallic Co further enhances the elec. cond. of the composite.  Also, the dominated capacitive contribution of SCCP electrode can also improve its lithium-storage performance.  Benefiting from the synergetic effects of these factors, when used as anode material for LIBs, SCCP demonstrates an ultrahigh specific capacity of 1009 mA h/g at 100 mA/g after 100 cycles.  Even at a high c.d. of 1000 mA/g, a reversible capacity of 462.8 mA-h/g is still achieved after 700 cycles.  SCCP should be a promising anode material for next generation LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqTCES9RZ0L4LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh6-2IPRR4aSw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXmsVWhu7s%253D&amp;md5=4909631818f5054718741b1efce5a66f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1002/smtd.201900231"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Polyanions Enhance Conversion Reactions for Lithium/Sodium-Ion Batteries: The Case of SbVO<sub>4</sub> Nanoparticles on Reduced Graphene Oxide</span>. <i>Small Methods</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>3</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">1900231</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/smtd.201900231</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D3%26publication_year%3D2019%26journal%3DSmall%2BMethods%26author%3DJ.%2BPan%26author%3DY.%2BZhang%26author%3DL.%2BLi%26author%3DZ.%2BCheng%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DX.%2BYang%26author%3DJ.%2BYang%26author%3DY.%2BQian%26title%3DPolyanions%2BEnhance%2BConversion%2BReactions%2Bfor%2BLithium%252FSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%253A%2BThe%2BCase%2Bof%2BSbVO4%2BNanoparticles%2Bon%2BReduced%2BGraphene%2BOxide%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fsmtd.201900231&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.0c21676&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fsmtd.201900231&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Polyanions Enhance Conversion Reactions for Lithium/Sodium-Ion Batteries: The Case of SbVO4 Nanoparticles on Reduced Graphene Oxide</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Jun; Zhang, Yuchen; Li, Lili; Cheng, Zhenjie; Li, Yanlu; Yang, Xianfeng; Yang, Jian; Qian, Yitai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small Methods</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1900231</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMMECI</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2366-9608</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Anode materials based on redox alloying/dealloying reactions are regarded as one of the promising electrodes in Li/Na-ion batteries.  However, the enormous vol. change upon cycling induces the giant structure strain, particle pulverization and then capacity decay.  Here, vanadates are proposed to mitigate this concern for alloy-type anode materials, using SbVO4 as an example.  As indicated by d. function theory and in situ/ex situ techniques, VO43- enhances the conversion reaction between Sb3+ and Sb, buffers the structure change induced by alloying/dealloying reactions of Sb and exhibits the electrochem. activity to Li ions.  These results make SbVO4 superior to Sb, Sb2O3 and SbPO4 in the electrochem. performances, which applies both to lithium-ion batteries and to sodium-ion batteries.  Then, the structure design and carbon composite are achieved by depositing monodispersed SbVO4 nanocrystals on reduced graphene oxides via a simple solvothermal reaction.  This composite shows a good cycling stability and a high rate capability, esp. in sodium-ion batteries (73.6% after 1500 cycles at 1 A g-1, or 252 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1).  These results open the door for other alloy-type anode materials to improve the performances.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoCysjsfxh3qrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgeGjPncrVaEA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXitVyhs7rJ&amp;md5=c88f2ba310f180d626dea4eb3b8ddb8c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2019.09.025"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Schulze, M.                 10.1016/j.ceramint.2018.04.133</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D44%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D13113-13121%26journal%3DCeram.%2BInt.%26author%3DB.%2BXiao%26author%3DB.%2BZhang%26author%3DJ.%2BZheng%26author%3DL.%2BTang%26author%3DC.%2BAn%26author%3DZ.%2BHe%26author%3DH.%2BTong%26author%3DW.%2BYu%26title%3DNano-Micro%2BStructure%2BVO2%252FCNTs%2BComposite%2Bas%2Ba%2BPotential%2BAnode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BLithium%2BIon%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.ceramint.2018.04.133&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.0c21676&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.ceramint.2018.04.133&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nano-microstructure VO2/CNTs composite as a potential anode material for lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiao, Bin; Zhang, Bao; Zheng, Jun-chao; Tang, Lin-bo; An, Chang-sheng; He, Zhen-jiang; Tong, Hui; Yu, Wan-jing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Ceramics International</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">44</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">13113-13121</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CINNDH</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0272-8842</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">VO2 is considered as a promising anode material for lithium ion batteries, owing to its high theor. capacity and fast ion-transfer rate.  However, the development of VO2 is hindered by the severe issues of poor elec. cond., large vol. changes and low energy d.  In this study, nano-microstructure VO2/CNTs spheres are well designed and successfully synthesized through a one-step solvothermal method, where the carbon nanotubes are inlayed throughout the whole microspheres.  This unique structure enables carbon nanotubes to improve the ion and electron cond. of VO2.  Besides, it can achieve a high tap d. (&gt; 1.3 g cm3) of VO2/CNTs electrode, which is higher than nanomaterials (&lt; 1.0 g cm3), and compatible with the current com. anode materials.  The Li+ storage behavior of VO2/CNTs is studied systematically in the potential range 0.01-3.0 V, it can obtain a high reversible specific capacity of 537.6 mA h g-1 at the c.d. of 0.05 A g-1.  Furthermore, the lithium insertion/extn. reaction mechanism of nano-microstructure VO2/CNTs is clarified.  The results demonstrate that the nano-microstructure relieves the vol. changes during charge/discharge cycling.  Therefore, it provides an insight to create functional materials with nano-microstructure for a wide range application.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrBobaD_LlJpLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgeGjPncrVaEA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXotFWnsb8%253D&amp;md5=0ff294142b003db157563345d3eab230</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2018.04.014"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhai, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Potassium Vanadate K<sub>0.23</sub>V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub> as Anode Materials for Lithium-Ion and Potassium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.
