                10.1016/j.jpowsour.2018.04.014</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D389%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D77-83%26journal%3DJ.%2BPower%2BSources%26author%3DC.%2BLiu%26author%3DS.%2BLuo%26author%3DH.%2BHuang%26author%3DZ.%2BWang%26author%3DQ.%2BWang%26author%3DY.%2BZhang%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DY.%2BZhai%26author%3DZ.%2BWang%26title%3DPotassium%2BVanadate%2BK0.23V2O5%2Bas%2BAnode%2BMaterials%2Bfor%2BLithium-Ion%2Band%2BPotassium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jpowsour.2018.04.014&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.0c21676&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jpowsour.2018.04.014&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Potassium vanadate K0.23V2O5 as anode materials for lithium-ion and potassium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Cailing; Luo, Shaohua; Huang, Hongbo; Wang, Zhiyuan; Wang, Qing; Zhang, Yahui; Liu, Yanguo; Zhai, Yuchun; Wang, Zhaowen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">389</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">77-83</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A layered potassium vanadate K0.23V2O5 has been successfully prepd. by the hydrothermal method and evaluated as an anode material for lithium-ion and potassium-ion batteries.  High structural stability is demonstrated by the ex situ X-ray diffraction (XRD) and ex situ SEM (SEM).  When used as an anode material for lithium-ion batteries, the K0.23V2O5 exhibits a reversible capacity of 480.4mAh g-1 at 20mAg-1 after 100 cycles and 439.7mAh g-1 at 200mAg-1 after 300 cycles as well as good cycling stability.  Even at a high c.d. of 800mAg-1, a high reversible capacity of 202.5mAh g-1 can be retained, indicating excellent rate performance.  Whereas in potassium-ion batteries, it retains a capacity of 121.6mAh g-1 after 150 cycles at 20mAg-1 and 97.6mAh g-1 at 100mAg-1 after 100 cycles.  Such superior electrochem. performance of K0.23V2O5 can be ascribed to the special flower-like morphol. and structure.  Overall, the results highlight the great potential of K0.23V2O5 as an anode material for both lithium-ion and potassium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqDmFdEaYtf9bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgeGjPncrVaEA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXnt1Srsrk%253D&amp;md5=2765a1979b98f2da969ae43aa07e8119</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref47'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201805227"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qu, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rueff, J.                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Layered-Structure SbPO4/Reduced Graphene Oxide: An Advanced Anode Material for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Jun; Chen, Shulin; Fu, Qiang; Sun, Yuanwei; Zhang, Yuchen; Lin, Na; Gao, Peng; Yang, Jian; Qian, Yitai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">12869-12878</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na ion batteries are one of most promising alternatives to Li ion batteries for large-scale energy storage, due to the high abundance and low cost of Na in the earth.  However, the lack of advanced electrode materials greatly affects their applications.  Here, layered-structure SbPO4 is explored as an anode material for Na ion batteries in terms of SbPO4 nanorods on reduced graphene oxide (SbPO4/rGO).  In situ transmission electron microscopy images reveal the preferential expansion along the transverse direction of the nanorods upon the first discharging, which arises from the redn. of SbPO4 to Sb and the subsequent alloying of Sb as supported by in situ x-ray diffraction and selected area electron diffraction patterns.  SbPO4/rGO exhibits a capacity retention of 99% after 100 cycles at 0.5 A/g both in half cells and in full cells.  Its specific capacity at 5 A/g is 214 mAh/g in half cells or 134 mAh/g in full cells.  The energy d. of the full cells at 1.2 KW/Kgtotal is still 99.8 Wh/Kgtotal, very promising as an advanced electrode material.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrQXjyU3XiANLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhLG023N5SVOw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemically active, novel layered m-ZnV2O6 nanobelts for highly rechargeable Na-ion energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Yan; Li, Chun-Sheng; Yang, Qiu-Ran; Chou, Shu-Lei; Liu, Hua-Kun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">205</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">62-69</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrode materials with a three-dimensional (3D) layered framework and excellent electrochem. stability can provide a new avenue for enhancing the overall performance of promising Na ion batteries.  Here, layered monoclinic (m) - ZnV2O6 nanobelts with high chem. activity for Na-ion energy storage were effectively fabricated via a rapid microwave irradn. method over the reaction time of 8 h, in which the fabricating efficiency is 24.5 times greater in comparison with the traditional hydrothermal method.  The morphol. and phase evolutions were verified by x-ray diffraction, SEM, and TEM.  This study also proposes the topotactic transformation-Ostwald ripening mechanism in layered m-ZnV2O6 nanobelts, from 1-dimensional (1D) m-Zn2V2O7 with tunnel structure to a 3-dimensional m-ZnV2O6 layered structure.  In particular, the m-ZnV2O6 nanobelt anode exhibited a high discharge capacity of 480.5 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 10 mA g-1, and maintained the considerable discharge capacity of 246.9 mAh g-1 at the 100th cycle.                 10.1016/j.jpowsour.2019.01.033</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D414%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D470-478%26journal%3DJ.%2BPower%2BSources%26author%3DT.%2BL.%2BNguyen%26author%3DT.%2BT.%2BSalunkhe%26author%3DT.%2BN.%2BVo%26author%3DH.%2BW.%2BChoi%26author%3DY.%2BC.%2BLee%26author%3DJ.%2BS.%2BChoi%26author%3DJ.%2BHur%26author%3DI.%2BT.%2BKim%26title%3DTailored%2BSynthesis%2Bof%2BAntimony-Based%2BAlloy%252FOxides%2BNanosheets%2Bfor%2BHigh-Performance%2BSodium-Ion%2BBattery%2BAnodes%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jpowsour.2019.01.033&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.0c21676&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jpowsour.2019.01.033&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tailored synthesis of antimony-based alloy/oxides nanosheets for high-performance sodium-ion battery anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nguyen, Tuan Loi; Salunkhe, Tejaswi Tanaji; Vo, Thuan Ngoc; Choi, Hyung Wook; Lee, Young-Chul; Choi, Jin-Seok; Hur, Jaehyun; Kim, Il Tae</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">414</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">470-478</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report a facile approach to synthesize NixSbyOz nanosheet mixts. consisting of Sb, Sb2O3 and NiSb2 for application as potential anode materials in sodium-ion batteries.  The reaction time affects the morphol., particle size, and phase components of the NixSbyOz nanosheet mixts.  The nanosheet mixt. (specifically, NixSbyOz-6h) exhibits an impressive electrochem. performance by demonstrating a remarkable cycling stability (over 250 cycles) with high coulombic efficiency (∼99%), reversible sodium storage capacity (∼382 mAh g-1), and excellent rate capability (∼315 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1).  The notable electrochem. performance can be ascribed to the presence of layered structures and the Ni inactive phase functioning as buffer spaces for the significant vol. expansion of Sb and preventing the collapse of the electrodes during the cycling process, as well as the shorter Na+ diffusion length, improving reaction kinetics.  Furthermore, to realize a potential full-cell, the nanosheet anode is combined with a Prussian blue NaxFeFe(CN)6 as a cathode, which exhibits a notable electrochem. performance with stable and high rate capacity by achieving an energy d. of ∼150 Wh kg-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpa5BY32-qY8bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhLG023N5SVOw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhsVShs7Y%253D&amp;md5=7725682e76bd819cd02bd878672d8107</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref52'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit52" data-doi="10.1021/am508670z"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Usui, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yoshioka, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wasada, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shimizu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sakaguchi, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nb-Doped Rutile TiO<sub>2</sub>: a Potential Anode Material for Na-Ion Battery</span>. <i>ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>7</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">6567</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">6573</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/am508670z</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D7%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D6567-6573%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BMater.%2BInterfaces%26author%3DH.%2BUsui%26author%3DS.%2BYoshioka%26author%3DK.%2BWasada%26author%3DM.%2BShimizu%26author%3DH.%2BSakaguchi%26title%3DNb-Doped%2BRutile%2BTiO2%253A%2Ba%2BPotential%2BAnode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BNa-Ion%2BBattery%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fam508670z&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.0c21676&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fam508670z&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nb-Doped Rutile TiO2: a Potential Anode Material for Na-Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Usui, Hiroyuki; Yoshioka, Sho; Wasada, Kuniaki; Shimizu, Masahiro; Sakaguchi, Hiroki</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6567-6573</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. properties of the rutile-type TiO2 and Nb-doped TiO2 were investigated for the first time as Na-ion battery anodes.  Ti1-xNbxO2 thick-film electrodes without a binder and a conductive additive were prepd. using a sol-gel method followed by a gas-deposition method.  The TiO2 electrode showed reversible reactions of Na insertion/extn. accompanied by expansion/contraction of the TiO2 lattice.  Among the Ti1-xNbxO2 electrodes with x = 0-0.18, the Ti0.94Nb0.06O2 electrode exhibited the best cycling performance, with a reversible capacity of 160 mA h g-1 at the 50th cycle.  As the Li-ion battery anode, this electrode also attained an excellent rate capability, with a capacity of 120 mA h g-1 even at the high c.d. of 16.75 A g-1 (50C).  The improvements in the performances are attributed to a 3 orders of magnitude higher electronic cond. of Ti0.94Nb0.06O2 compared to that of TiO2.  This offers the possibility of Nb-doped rutile TiO2 as a Na-ion battery anode as well as a Li-ion battery anode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr_obY7X6IHJrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhLG023N5SVOw"> &gt;&gt;     </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrochem. insertion of sodium ions into carbon using solid polymer electrolytes or org. liq. electrolytes is described.  Cells with the configuration Na/P(EO)6NaCF3SO3/CP(EO) (PEO = polyethylene oxide) or Na/liq. electrolyte/C were galvanostatically discharged, charged, and cycled.  The extent of insertion into C (i.e., x in Na+Cax-) was found to be a strong function of the type and particle size of the carbon used, and the reversibility of the process was highly dependent upon the type of electrolyte used.  The possibility of design a sodium ion rocking chair cell is discussed, and a first-generation example, using a petroleum coke anode, polymer electrolyte, and sodium cobalt bronze cathode is described.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGocbintpirKnrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh5um7v-wodkQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaK2cXhsVKqu7o%253D&amp;md5=a50a9d5ed6dd7cc569094cf9ab06beb4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201600943"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Energy prodn. and storage technologies have attracted a great deal of attention for day-to-day applications.  In recent decades, advances in lithium-ion battery (LIB) technol. have improved living conditions around the globe.  LIBs are used in most mobile electronic devices as well as in zero-emission electronic vehicles.  However, there are increasing concerns regarding load leveling of renewable energy sources and the smart grid as well as the sustainability of lithium sources due to their limited availability and consequent expected price increase.  Therefore, whether LIBs alone can satisfy the rising demand for small- and/or mid-to-large-format energy storage applications remains unclear.  To mitigate these issues, recent research has focused on alternative energy storage systems.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as the best candidate power sources because sodium is widely available and exhibits similar chem. to that of LIBs; therefore, SIBs are promising next-generation alternatives.  Recently, sodiated layer transition metal oxides, phosphates and org. compds. have been introduced as cathode materials for SIBs.  Simultaneously, recent developments have been facilitated by the use of select carbonaceous materials, transition metal oxides (or sulfides), and intermetallic and org. compds. as anodes for SIBs.  Apart from electrode materials, suitable electrolytes, additives, and binders are equally important for the development of practical SIBs.  Despite developments in electrode materials and other components, there remain several challenges, including cell design and electrode balancing, in the application of sodium ion cells.  In this article, we summarize and discuss current research on materials and propose future directions for SIBs.  This will provide important insights into scientific and practical issues in the development of SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGot-2IKXj-Q-7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh5um7v-wodkQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXkvF2rsbk%253D&amp;md5=cfc7b2d153696dcbded22d954ff06174</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref7" class="rightTabRefNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit7" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201800930"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, H.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have emerged in recent years, due to their advantages of natural abundance, low cost and environmental friendliness.  In this article, we review the up-to-date research progress on anode materials for Na-ion batteries from five respects: carbon-based materials, alloy-based materials, metal oxides and sulfides based on conversion reaction, titanium-based compds. with insertion mechanism, and org. composites.  In particular, we not only summarize the Na-storage mechanism of these anodes, but also discuss the failure mechanism.  The problems and challenges assocd. with these anodes are pointed out.  Furthermore, on the basis of extensive reports and our exptl. studies, feasible strategies are suggested for designing high performance anode materials.  After further in-depth exploration and investigation, we believe that Na-ion batteries are promising alternative to lithium-ion batteries for low cost and large-scale energy storage systems in the near future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrB4Pf2vZ5QrrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh5um7v-wodkQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFelsrnN&amp;md5=8311789a2dc4e61dabff177245235c3e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref9" class="rightTabRefNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit9" data-doi="10.1021/jz2012066"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Slater, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are an attractive alternative to lithium-ion batteries that alleviate problems with lithium availability and cost.  Despite several studies of cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries involving layered oxide materials, there are few low-voltage metal oxide anodes capable of operating sodium ion reversibly at room temp.  We have synthesized amorphous titanium dioxide nanotube electrodes directly grown on current collectors without binders and additives to use as an anode for sodium-ion batteries.  We find that only amorphous large diam. nanotubes (&gt;80 nm I.D.) can support electrochem. cycling with sodium ions.  These electrodes maximize their capacity in operando and reach reversible capacity of 150 mA-h/g in 15 cycles.  We also demonstrate for the first time a full cell all-oxide sodium-ion battery using amorphous titanium dioxide nanotube anode coupled to a Na1.0Li0.2Ni0.25Mn0.75Oδ cathode at room temp. exhibiting good rate capability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr8q2bDG7YJCbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh5um7v-wodkQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXht1ChtLbP&amp;md5=66a2a71991a01d6823c9c01024f65c74</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref10" class="rightTabRefNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit10" data-doi="10.1021/nl402747x"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, K.         </div><div class="casAbstract">We report the electrochem. activity of anatase TiO2 nanorods in a Na cell.  The anatase TiO2 nanorods were synthesized by a hydrothermal method, and their surfaces were coated by carbon to improve the elec. cond. by carbonization of pitch at 700° for 2 h in Ar flow.  The resulting structure does not change before and after the carbon coating, as confirmed by x-ray diffraction.  Transmission electron microscopy images confirm the presence of a carbon coating on the anatase TiO2 nanorods.  In cell tests, anodes of bare and carbon-coated anatase TiO2 nanorods exhibit stable cycling performance and attain a capacity of about 172 and 193 mA-h/g on the first charge, resp., in the voltage range of 0-3 V.  With the help of the conductive carbon layers, the carbon-coated anatase TiO2 delivers more capacity at high rates, 104 mA-h/g at the 10C rate (3.3 A/g), 82 mA-h/g at the 30C rate (10 A/g), and 53 mA-h/g at the 100C rate (33 A g-1).  By contrast, the anode of bare anatase TiO2 nanorods delivers only about 38 mA-h/g at the 10C rate (3.3 A/g).  The excellent cyclability and high-rate capability are the result of a Na+ insertion and extn. reaction into the host structure coupled with Ti4+/3+ redox reaction, as shown by x-ray absorption spectroscopy.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpadjcIpWM-W7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh5um7v-wodkQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXktlGhsA%253D%253D&amp;md5=4bc3a520e6f654a82cbee3b778eef0e7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref11" class="rightTabRefNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit11" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201904398"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Meng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mai, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Niu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">An, Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Vanadium-Based Nanomaterials: A Promising Family for Emerging Metal-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The emerging electrochem. energy storage systems beyond Li-ion batteries, including Na/K/Mg/Ca/Zn/Al-ion batteries, attract extensive interest as the development of Li-ion batteries is seriously hindered by the scarce Li resources.  During the past years, large amts. of studies have focused on the study of various electrode materials toward emerging metal-ion batteries to realize high energy d., high power d., and a long cycle life.  In particular, V-based nanomaterials have received great attention.  V-based compds. have a big family with different structures, chem. compns., and electrochem. properties, which provide huge possibilities for the development of emerging electrochem. energy storage.  In this review, a comprehensive overview of the recent progresses of promising V-based nanomaterials for emerging metal-ion batteries is presented.  The V-based materials are classified into four groups: V oxides, vanadates, V phosphates, and O-free V-based compds.  The structures, electrochem. properties, and modification strategies are discussed.  The structure-performance relations and charge storage mechanisms are focused on.  Finally, the perspectives about future directions of V-based nanomaterials for emerging energy storage devices are proposed.  This review will provide comprehensive knowledge of V-based nanomaterials and shed light on their potential applications in emerging energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqTA_FmH74ksbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh5um7v-wodkQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXmt1SqtQ%253D%253D&amp;md5=02ae2332840446c0a2e6dbdbfb2021cd</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref12" class="rightTabRefNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit12" data-doi="10.1021/nl500915b"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Niu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Meng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mai, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">VO<sub>2</sub> Nanowires Assembled into Hollow Microspheres for High-Rate and Long-Life Lithium Batteries</span>. <i>Nano Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>14</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2873</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2878</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Development of 3-dimensional nanostructures with high surface area and excellent structural stability is an important approach for realizing high-rate and long-life battery electrodes.  Here, the authors report VO2 hollow microspheres showing empty spherical core with radially protruding nanowires, synthesized through a facile and controllable ion-modulating approach.  By controlling the self-assembly of neg. charged C12H25SO4- spherical micelles and pos. charged VO2+ ions, 6-armed microspindles and random nanowires are also prepd.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The binary transition metal oxides have attracted great attention because of their considerable energy and power densities.  However, they suffer from low reaction kinetics and large vol. change, limiting their practical energy applications.  The construction of a mesoporous structure with a large surface area, the development of a carbon matrix, as well as heteroatom doping can effectively overcome the above challenges.  Herein, the synthesis of phosphorous-contg. Fe2VO4/nitrogen-doped carbon mesoporous nanowires (P-Fe2VO4/NCMNWs) is reported.  In this unique structure, the at.-level P-doping could increase the cond. of Fe2VO4 by reducing its band gap, which is confirmed by DFT calcns.  Furthermore, the phosphorus can covalently "bridge" the carbon layer and Fe2VO4 through P-C and Fe-O-P bondings. Therefore, this review discusses the basic theories and application bottlenecks of multi-electron mechanisms from the view of thermodn. and dynamic principles.  In future, high-energy batteries, metal anodes and multi-electron cathodes are promising electrode materials with high theor. capacity and high output voltage.  While the primary issue for the multi-electron transfer process is sluggish kinetics, which may be caused by multiple ionic migration, large ionic radius, high reaction energy barrier, low electron cond., poor structural stability, etc., it is urgent that feasible and versatile modification methods are summarized and new inspiration proposed in order to break through kinetic constraints. In addn., the conversion reaction product of amorphous Na2O display their better chem. stability than amorphous Li2O during electrochem. cycles, which contribute to a stable and long cycling life of NIBs.  This work gain insight into the high-capacity anodes with conversation-alloying mechanism for NIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqYH6L4bixii7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgIGKrcsM_7hg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXltVKkurY%253D&amp;md5=2801580dae4365a2e10c3bdd3b4bb313</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref24" class="rightTabRefNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit24" data-doi="10.1039/C9TA07508A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ouyang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Phosphorus and Carbon Composite Containing Nanocrystalline Sb as a Stable and High-Capacity Anode for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries are a potential alternative to lithium ion batteries due to the low cost and natural abundance of sodium.  In this study, the synthesis is demonstrated of a ternary Sb/P-C composite by using facile discharge plasma-assisted milling (P-milling) to combine Sb and high theor. specific capacity red phosphorus (RP).  The high hardness Sb particles facilitated the refinement of the P particles and exfoliated expanded graphite during the P-milling process, while the rapid heating by plasma promoted the refinement of Sb and P particles.  Ultimately, the cryst. Sb nanograins were well-dispersed in the amorphous P and C matrix, and the P and C components were connected by the P-C bonds.  This unique structure ensures a strong electrode structural integrity and ultra-fast electron transport during cycling.  As a result, the Sb/P-C composite delivered a high av. initial coulombic efficiency of 73.5%, and a reversible capacity of 596 mA h g-1 after 300 cycles at 1.0 A g-1, a very impressive performance among the reported P-based materials.  The present approach provides a new strategy for the prepn. of anode materials of high capacity and long cycle life for sodium-ion batteries and other energy storage systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrmDND1n2Yqi7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgIGKrcsM_7hg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXitlSqtrzM&amp;md5=dd0ad28a88cccfe001142bead705025e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref25" class="rightTabRefNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit25" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2020.104532"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ye, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, R.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Curbing Polysulfide Shuttling by Synergistic Engineering Layer Composed of Supported Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> Nanodots Electrocatalyst in Lithium-Sulfur Batteries</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>70</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">104532</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

Herein, we report a synergistic engineering layer composed of acorn shell porous carbon/Sn4P3 nanodots electrocatalyst (AS PC-Sn4P3).  The synergistic engineering layer can not only serve as a conductive interface but also provide a dual-adsorption barrier to retain active material and inhibit the LiPSs migrating.  More importantly, electrocatalytic Sn4P3 nanodots supported on acorn shell porous carbon (AS PC) within synergistic engineering layer effectively promote lithium ion diffusion, LiPSs conversion, Li2S2/Li2S deposition, and accelerate the electrochem. redox reaction and therefore curb the sol. However, the use of Sn4P3 has been impeded by capacity fade and an inferior rate performance. Such obtained Sb2O3/rGO composite demonstrates a highly reversible specific capacity (1355 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1), good rate capability, and superior life cycle (525 mA h g-1 after 700 cycles at 600 mA g-1) when used as anodes for Li-ion batteries (LIBs). Also, these findings are helpful in both developing novel high-performance electrodes for LIBs and synthesizing functional materials in an ecofriendly and economical way.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqEirQnR3m7ELVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lia2k7905UxKA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhsFeiur7I&amp;md5=883fd2447825522833629d534aa1d08f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref30" class="rightTabRefNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit30" data-doi="10.1016/S0378-7753(01)00964-8"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Study of Surface Films Formed on SnO Anode in Lithium Rechargeable Batteries by FTIR Spectroscopy</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">MXenes, a novel family of two dimensional (2D) materials with excellent electronic cond. and hydrophilicity, have emerged as a promising material for energy storage.  Based on the intercalation mechanism, MXenes have demonstrated an excellent performance for supercapacitors but low capacities for sodium-ion batteries.  Herein, we developed a facile soln.-phase method to fabricate the Sb2O3/MXene(Ti3C2Tx) hybrid materials for sodium storage with enhanced electrochem. performances.  The as-prepd. Sb2O3/Ti3C2Tx composite has a hierarchical structure with Sb2O3 nanoparticles (sub-50 nm) uniformly incorporated in the MXene Ti3C2Tx 3D networks.  The Sb2O3 nanoparticles serve as a sufficient sodium ion reservoir; meanwhile, the MXene Ti3C2Tx network provides highly efficient pathways for transport of electrons and Na-ions.  The vol. expansion of Sb2O3 during sodiation/desodiation can be buffered and confined between the 2D Ti3C2Tx sheets.  As a result, the Sb2O3/Ti3C2Tx hybrid anodes present good structural stability and superior electrochem. performance in Na-ion batteries, including an excellent rate performance with a capacity of 295 mA h g-1 at 2 A g-1, and an enhanced cycling performance with a capacity of 472 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles at 100 mA g-1. In this unique structure, both ends of Sb2O3 nanoribbons with the thickness of ∼50 nm scatter with each other and extend radially from the center point, which not only reserves more space between nanoribbons to accommodate vol. changes, but also provides plenty of open channels to facilitate the intimate contact of active species, conductive agents and electrolytes, thus efficiently shortening diffusion paths of Na+/e-.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na ion batteries (SIBs) have been considered a promising alternative to Li ion batteries for large-scale energy storage.  However, their inferior electrochem. performances, esp. cyclability, become the major challenge for further development of SIBs.  Large vol. change and sluggish diffusion kinetics are generally considered to be responsible for the fast capacity degrdn.  We report the strong chem. bonding of nanostructured Sb2S3 on S-doped graphene sheets (Sb2S3/SGS) that enables a stable capacity retention of 83% for 900 cycles with high capacities and excellent rate performances.  To the best of our knowledge, the cycling performance of the Sb2S3/SGS composite is superior to those reported for any other Sb-based materials for SIBs.  Computational calcns. demonstrate that S-doped graphene (SGS) has a stronger affinity for Sb2S3 and the discharge products than pure graphene, resulting in a robust composite architecture for outstanding cycling stability.  Our study shows a feasible and effective way to solve the long-term cycling stability issue for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqCGE30ZIPm4bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhLb6XJ8xWAPg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitVGnsbnM&amp;md5=bf18bc0bdfb7f9241bfba0fe990d1c93</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref36" class="rightTabRefNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit36" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2019.103965"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ye, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, R.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Exceptional Adsorption and Catalysis Effects of Hollow Polyhedra/Carbon Nanotube Confined CoP Nanoparticles Superstructures for Enhanced Lithium-Sulfur Batteries</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>64</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">103965</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Lithium-sulfur (Li-S) batteries with high theor. energy d. are promising next-generation green energy storage devices.  However, the severe shuttling and depressed conversion of lithium polysulfides in sulfur cathode are two pivotal factors that limit the practical application of Li-S batteries.  To solve these issues, rationally designed hollow polyhedra/carbon nanotube confined CoP nanoparticles superstructures (CoP@HPCN) for enhanced Li-S batteries are proposed here.  With the high porosity and cavity, and multidirectional channels, hollow polyhedra/carbon nanotube architecture can effectively accommodate vol. expansion and entrap sulfur species.  More importantly, the exptl. and theor. results indicate that the uniformly inserted polar CoP nanoparticles as electrocatalyst not only significantly anchor polysulfides, but also catalyze the transformation of lithium polysulfides.  Benefiting from these advantages, the CoP@HPCN based sulfur cathode can achieve good rate performance, impressive cycling stability, and ultralow self-discharge const. of 0.03% per day after resting for 60 days even at high sulfur loading of 3.7 mg cm-2.  This work synergistically combines desired design and electrocatalysis in sulfur electrode and sheds some light on the construction of advanced Li-S batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqlZ1vJ5Z-rp7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhLb6XJ8xWAPg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhsFGjsLvO&amp;md5=366291ef2f391836252eba32fbedf795</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref37" class="rightTabRefNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit37" data-doi="10.1038/35035045"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Poizot, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Laruelle, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Grugeon, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dupont, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tarascon, J.                         rightTab-cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nano-sized transition-metal oxides as negative-electrode materials for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Poizot P; Laruelle S; Grugeon S; Dupont L; Tarascon J M</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature</span>

    </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable solid-state batteries have long been considered an attractive power source for a wide variety of applications, and in particular, lithium-ion batteries are emerging as the technology of choice for portable electronics.  One of the main challenges in the design of these batteries is to ensure that the electrodes maintain their integrity over many discharge-recharge cycles.  Although promising electrode systems have recently been proposed, their lifespans are limited by Li-alloying agglomeration or the growth of passivation layers, which prevent the fully reversible insertion of Li ions into the negative electrodes.  Here we report that electrodes made of nanoparticles of transition-metal oxides (MO, where M is Co, Ni, Cu or Fe) demonstrate electrochemical capacities of 700 mA h g(-1), with 100% capacity retention for up to 100 cycles and high recharging rates.  The mechanism of Li reactivity differs from the classical Li insertion/deinsertion or Li-alloying processes, and involves the formation and decomposition of Li2O, accompanying the reduction and oxidation of metal nanoparticles (in the range 1-5 nanometres) respectively.  We expect that the use of transition-metal nanoparticles to enhance surface electrochemical reactivity will lead to further improvements in the performance of lithium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcTITCWEoR0MQxfKb6ELK8t0fW6udTcc2eb7Q2zs98s4x7ntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BD3cvnslKhtQ%253D%253D&amp;md5=5a244324b84031fe58b67cdc4038c56c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref38" class="rightTabRefNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit38" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201202623"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Reconstruction of Conformal Nanoscale MnO on Graphene as a High-Capacity and Long-Life Anode Material for Lithium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. The prepd. MnO/graphene hybrid anode exhibits a reversible capacity as high as 2014.1 mAh g-1 after 150 discharge/charge cycles at 200 mA g-1, excellent rate capability (625.8 mAh g-1 at 3000 mA g-1), and superior cyclability (843.3 mAh g-1 even after 400 discharge/charge cycles at 2000 mA g-1 with only 0.01% capacity loss per cycle).         </div><div class="casAbstract">Taking advantage of zeolitic imidazolate framework (ZIF-8), ZnS-Sb2S3@C core-double shell polyhedron structure is synthesized through a sulfurization reaction between Zn2+ dissocd. from ZIF-8 and S2- from thioacetamide (TAA), and subsequently a metal cation exchange process between Zn2+ and Sb3+, in which carbon layer is introduced from polymeric resorcinol-formaldehyde to prevent the collapse of the polyhedron.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Pure micrometric antimony can be successfully used as neg. electrode material in Na-ion batteries, sustaining a capacity close to 600 mAh g-1 at a high rate with a Coulombic efficiency of 99 over 160 cycles, an extremely high capacity compared to any other compd. tested against both Li and Na.  The reaction mechanism with Na does not simply go through the alloying mechanism obsd. for Li where the intermediate species are those expected from the phase diagram.  In the case of Na, the intermediate phases are mostly amorphous and could not be precisely identified.  Surprisingly, it is evidenced that a competition takes place at the end of the discharge of the Sb/Na cell between the formation of the hexagonal and the cubic polymorphs of Na3Sb, the last being described in the literature as unstable at atm. pressure and only synthesized under high pressure (1-9 GPa).         </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony-based oxides (SbxOy) were considered as promising candidate anode materials for lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  However, the poor elec. cond. and huge vol. change of SbxOy during lithium insertion and extn. hinder its lithium-storage performance.  Sb2O5/Co-contg. carbon polyhedra (SCCP) were prepd. through a galvanic replacement reaction accompanied by oxidn. process.  Sb2O5 possesses high theor. capacity and carbon not only effectively improves the charge transport ability but also accommodates the vol. change of Sb2O5 during charge/discharge process.  Besides, the inner metallic Co further enhances the elec. cond. of the composite.  Also, the dominated capacitive contribution of SCCP electrode can also improve its lithium-storage performance.  Benefiting from the synergetic effects of these factors, when used as anode material for LIBs, SCCP demonstrates an ultrahigh specific capacity of 1009 mA h/g at 100 mA/g after 100 cycles.  Even at a high c.d. of 1000 mA/g, a reversible capacity of 462.8 mA-h/g is still achieved after 700 cycles.  SCCP should be a promising anode material for next generation LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqTCES9RZ0L4LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhLb6XJ8xWAPg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXmsVWhu7s%253D&amp;md5=4909631818f5054718741b1efce5a66f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref42" class="rightTabRefNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit42" data-doi="10.1002/smtd.201900231"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Polyanions Enhance Conversion Reactions for Lithium/Sodium-Ion Batteries: The Case of SbVO<sub>4</sub> Nanoparticles on Reduced Graphene Oxide</span>. <i>Small Methods</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>3</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">1900231</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        rightTab-cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Polyanions Enhance Conversion Reactions for Lithium/Sodium-Ion Batteries: The Case of SbVO4 Nanoparticles on Reduced Graphene Oxide</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Jun; Zhang, Yuchen; Li, Lili; Cheng, Zhenjie; Li, Yanlu; Yang, Xianfeng; Yang, Jian; Qian, Yitai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small Methods</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1900231</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Anode materials based on redox alloying/dealloying reactions are regarded as one of the promising electrodes in Li/Na-ion batteries.  However, the enormous vol. change upon cycling induces the giant structure strain, particle pulverization and then capacity decay.  Here, vanadates are proposed to mitigate this concern for alloy-type anode materials, using SbVO4 as an example.  As indicated by d. function theory and in situ/ex situ techniques, VO43- enhances the conversion reaction between Sb3+ and Sb, buffers the structure change induced by alloying/dealloying reactions of Sb and exhibits the electrochem. activity to Li ions.  These results make SbVO4 superior to Sb, Sb2O3 and SbPO4 in the electrochem. performances, which applies both to lithium-ion batteries and to sodium-ion batteries.  Then, the structure design and carbon composite are achieved by depositing monodispersed SbVO4 nanocrystals on reduced graphene oxides via a simple solvothermal reaction.  This composite shows a good cycling stability and a high rate capability, esp. in sodium-ion batteries (73.6% after 1500 cycles at 1 A g-1, or 252 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1).  These results open the door for other alloy-type anode materials to improve the performances.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoCysjsfxh3qrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li-ywPt4bW1MA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXitVyhs7rJ&amp;md5=c88f2ba310f180d626dea4eb3b8ddb8c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref43" class="rightTabRefNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit43" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2019.09.025"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Schulze, M.                         rightTab-cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nano-microstructure VO2/CNTs composite as a potential anode material for lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiao, Bin; Zhang, Bao; Zheng, Jun-chao; Tang, Lin-bo; An, Chang-sheng; He, Zhen-jiang; Tong, Hui; Yu, Wan-jing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Ceramics International</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">VO2 is considered as a promising anode material for lithium ion batteries, owing to its high theor. capacity and fast ion-transfer rate.  However, the development of VO2 is hindered by the severe issues of poor elec. cond., large vol. changes and low energy d.  In this study, nano-microstructure VO2/CNTs spheres are well designed and successfully synthesized through a one-step solvothermal method, where the carbon nanotubes are inlayed throughout the whole microspheres.  This unique structure enables carbon nanotubes to improve the ion and electron cond. of VO2.  Besides, it can achieve a high tap d. (&gt; 1.3 g cm3) of VO2/CNTs electrode, which is higher than nanomaterials (&lt; 1.0 g cm3), and compatible with the current com. anode materials.  The Li+ storage behavior of VO2/CNTs is studied systematically in the potential range 0.01-3.0 V, it can obtain a high reversible specific capacity of 537.6 mA h g-1 at the c.d. of 0.05 A g-1.  Furthermore, the lithium insertion/extn. reaction mechanism of nano-microstructure VO2/CNTs is clarified.  The results demonstrate that the nano-microstructure relieves the vol. changes during charge/discharge cycling.  Therefore, it provides an insight to create functional materials with nano-microstructure for a wide range application.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrBobaD_LlJpLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li-ywPt4bW1MA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXotFWnsb8%253D&amp;md5=0ff294142b003db157563345d3eab230</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref46" class="rightTabRefNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit46" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2018.04.014"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhai, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Potassium Vanadate K<sub>0.23</sub>V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub> as Anode Materials for Lithium-Ion and Potassium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         rightTab-cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Potassium vanadate K0.23V2O5 as anode materials for lithium-ion and potassium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Cailing; Luo, Shaohua; Huang, Hongbo; Wang, Zhiyuan; Wang, Qing; Zhang, Yahui; Liu, Yanguo; Zhai, Yuchun; Wang, Zhaowen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A layered potassium vanadate K0.23V2O5 has been successfully prepd. by the hydrothermal method and evaluated as an anode material for lithium-ion and potassium-ion batteries.  High structural stability is demonstrated by the ex situ X-ray diffraction (XRD) and ex situ SEM (SEM).  When used as an anode material for lithium-ion batteries, the K0.23V2O5 exhibits a reversible capacity of 480.4mAh g-1 at 20mAg-1 after 100 cycles and 439.7mAh g-1 at 200mAg-1 after 300 cycles as well as good cycling stability.  Even at a high c.d. of 800mAg-1, a high reversible capacity of 202.5mAh g-1 can be retained, indicating excellent rate performance.  Whereas in potassium-ion batteries, it retains a capacity of 121.6mAh g-1 after 150 cycles at 20mAg-1 and 97.6mAh g-1 at 100mAg-1 after 100 cycles.  Such superior electrochem. performance of K0.23V2O5 can be ascribed to the special flower-like morphol. and structure.  Overall, the results highlight the great potential of K0.23V2O5 as an anode material for both lithium-ion and potassium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqDmFdEaYtf9bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li-ywPt4bW1MA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXnt1Srsrk%253D&amp;md5=2765a1979b98f2da969ae43aa07e8119</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref47" class="rightTabRefNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit47" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201805227"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qu, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rueff, J.                 10.1021/acsnano.8b08065</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Layered-Structure SbPO4/Reduced Graphene Oxide: An Advanced Anode Material for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Jun; Chen, Shulin; Fu, Qiang; Sun, Yuanwei; Zhang, Yuchen; Lin, Na; Gao, Peng; Yang, Jian; Qian, Yitai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na ion batteries are one of most promising alternatives to Li ion batteries for large-scale energy storage, due to the high abundance and low cost of Na in the earth.  However, the lack of advanced electrode materials greatly affects their applications.  Here, layered-structure SbPO4 is explored as an anode material for Na ion batteries in terms of SbPO4 nanorods on reduced graphene oxide (SbPO4/rGO).  In situ transmission electron microscopy images reveal the preferential expansion along the transverse direction of the nanorods upon the first discharging, which arises from the redn. of SbPO4 to Sb and the subsequent alloying of Sb as supported by in situ x-ray diffraction and selected area electron diffraction patterns.  SbPO4/rGO exhibits a capacity retention of 99% after 100 cycles at 0.5 A/g both in half cells and in full cells.  Its specific capacity at 5 A/g is 214 mAh/g in half cells or 134 mAh/g in full cells.  The energy d. of the full cells at 1.2 KW/Kgtotal is still 99.8 Wh/Kgtotal, very promising as an advanced electrode material.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrQXjyU3XiANLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li-ywPt4bW1MA"> &gt;&gt;
